<div id="" class="hds-image-of-the-day color-mode-light hds-color-mode-light hds-module hds-module-full alignfull wp-block-nasa-blocks-image-of-the-day">
	<div class="grid-container grid-container-block padding-y-9 padding-x-3">
		<div class="grid-row">
			<div class="grid-col-12 desktop:grid-col-4 desktop:padding-right-5 margin-bottom-6 desktop:margin-bottom-0">
				<div class="margin-bottom-10 display-none tablet:display-block desktop:display-block">
					<h3 class="label">Today</h3>
					<h2 class="display-41 margin-0">Image Of The Day</h2>
				</div>
				<p class="heading-22 margin-bottom-2">Putting the X-59 to the Test</p>
				<p class="p-md">Researchers from NASA and the Japanese Aerospace Exploration Agency (JAXA) recently tested a scale model of the X-59 experimental aircraft in a supersonic wind tunnel located in Chofu, Japan, to assess the noise audible underneath the aircraft. The test was an important milestone for NASA’s one-of-a-kind X-59, which is designed to fly faster than the speed of sound without causing a loud sonic boom.</p>
				<div className="margin-top-1 margin-bottom-1">
							<a href="https://www.nasa.gov/image-of-the-day/" target="_self" class="button-primary button-primary-sm link-external-false">
			<span class="line-height-alt-1 " >
				Browse Image Archive                			</span>
			<svg viewBox="0 0 32 32" fill="none" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg"><circle class="button-primary-circle" cx="16" cy="16" r="16"></circle><path d="M8 16.956h12.604l-3.844 4.106 1.252 1.338L24 16l-5.988-6.4-1.252 1.338 3.844 4.106H8v1.912z" class="color-spacesuit-white"></path></svg>
		</a>
					</div>
			</div>
			<div class="grid-col-12 desktop:grid-col-8 desktop:padding-left-5">
				<div class="margin-bottom-2 display-block tablet:display-none desktop:display-none">
					<h3 class="label">Today</h3>
					<h2 class="display-41 margin-0">Image Of The Day</h2>
				</div>

				<div class="margin-bottom-2">
					<h3 class="subtitle-md">Earth Information Center</h3>
				</div>
				<div class="margin-bottom-2">
					<h2 class="display-48">Explore our changing planet</h2>
				</div>
				<div class="margin-bottom-2">
					<p class="heading-18 line-height-md"></p>
				</div>
				<p class="p-md">For more than 50 years, NASA satellites have provided data on Earth&#8217;s land, water, air, temperature, and climate. NASA&#8217;s Earth Information Center allows visitors to see how our planet is changing in six key areas: sea level rise and coastal impacts, health and air quality, wildfires, greenhouse gases, sustainable energy, and agriculture.</p>
				<a href="https://earth.gov/" target="_self" class="button-primary button-primary-md" rel="noopener">
					<span class="line-height-alt-1">
                        Earth Science <span class="usa-sr-only">about Explore our changing planet</span>                    </span>
					<svg viewBox="0 0 32 32" fill="none" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg"><circle class="button-primary-circle" cx="16" cy="16" r="16"></circle><path d="M8 16.956h12.604l-3.844 4.106 1.252 1.338L24 16l-5.988-6.4-1.252 1.338 3.844 4.106H8v1.912z" class="color-spacesuit-white"></path></svg>
				</a>
			</div>
			<div class="grid-col-12 desktop:grid-col-6 desktop:padding-left-5">
				<div class="width-full display-block">
					<div class="hds-media-wrapper margin-left-auto margin-right-auto"><figure class="hds-media-inner hds-cover-wrapper hds-media-ratio-cover "><img loading="lazy" decoding="async" width="1446" height="964" src="https://www.nasa.gov/wp-content/uploads/2025/07/bloom-pce-20250621-lrg.jpg?w=1446" class="attachment-1536x1536 size-1536x1536" alt="" style="transform: scale(1); transform-origin: 31% 36%; object-position: 31% 36%; object-fit: cover;" block_context="nasa-block" srcset="https://www.nasa.gov/wp-content/uploads/2025/07/bloom-pce-20250621-lrg.jpg 1446w, https://www.nasa.gov/wp-content/uploads/2025/07/bloom-pce-20250621-lrg.jpg?resize=300,200 300w, https://www.nasa.gov/wp-content/uploads/2025/07/bloom-pce-20250621-lrg.jpg?resize=768,512 768w, https://www.nasa.gov/wp-content/uploads/2025/07/bloom-pce-20250621-lrg.jpg?resize=1024,683 1024w, https://www.nasa.gov/wp-content/uploads/2025/07/bloom-pce-20250621-lrg.jpg?resize=400,267 400w, https://www.nasa.gov/wp-content/uploads/2025/07/bloom-pce-20250621-lrg.jpg?resize=600,400 600w, https://www.nasa.gov/wp-content/uploads/2025/07/bloom-pce-20250621-lrg.jpg?resize=900,600 900w, https://www.nasa.gov/wp-content/uploads/2025/07/bloom-pce-20250621-lrg.jpg?resize=1200,800 1200w" sizes="auto, (max-width: 1446px) 100vw, 1446px" /></figure><figcaption class="hds-caption padding-y-2"><div class="hds-caption-text p-sm margin-0">A type of phytoplankton called coccolithophores, less common in waters off New England since around 2010, made an impressive appearance in summer 2025.</div></figcaption></div>				</div>
